  242. I really wanted to write a review of this product as I have been the proud owner of one for over 5 years.<br /><br />Let me begin by saying why I ordered one. I learned how to give haircuts while I was in high school and after I went to college I gave a few haircuts every now and then using other people's clippers. My friends finally convinced me to invest in a clipper, since I was the only one on my floor that knew how to give haircuts. I knew Oster was a good make and I really wanted to get a good, long-lasting clipper. I was vacillating between this one and the Classic 76 which I personally knew to be a quality clipper. To be honest, I was a little skeptical buying this one because it was less than half the price of the Classic 76 (as well as only 12 watts in comparison to the 76's 26 watts) which sort-of led me to believe it was not as good. I finally decided to try this one out and rationalized that at least I could make my money back on it and then save up a bit to buy the Classic 76 if need be. I ordered the T-Finisher to compliment my set, as well as a carrying case to hold all my stuff together. All-in-all, I spent about $120. Let me tell you, when I first used this clipper, it was love at first cut. It cut like a hot knife through butter and I was easily able to give about 5 haircuts an hour. I charged cheap for my haircuts, about $5 a pop, and I can't tell you how long the lines were waiting for me to give haircuts. I had given over a hundred haircuts already (obviously lubricating the blades every now-and-then to keep it smoothe), and it was still going strong. I still wasn't convinced that the blades would last that much longer, so I made sure to set aside some money to buy Classic 76 when this one broke down. Well, let me tell you, after 3 years of college (I graduated early) this clipper was amazing and worked like the day I got it. After I got married and moved out, I slowly built a small-scale haircutting business on the side, with myFast Feed Clipper in hand. Co-workers, family, and friends were all customers of mine and they were most impressed with the job I did as well as the smootheness of the clipper.<br /><br />All-in-all after about 5 years of owning this clipper and over 1000 haircuts with it, I can honestly say this was probably the best investment I ever made. I'm happy I didn't end up going with the Classic 76, because this one suited my needs just fine at less than half the price!<br /><br />The only downsides I can think of is that the clipper gets very hot after using it for over an hour. I got too freaked out to continue using it and usually didn't give more than 6 or 7 haircuts in a row before letting the thing cool down for a while, so I can't tell you if it would destroy the motor if you used it longer. The other downside is that it only comes with 4 or 5 guards and they aren't the best quality. After a while, I bought the spring-loaded guards rather than just the ones that slip onto the clipper and I was set.<br /><br />To sum it up in one sentence: Great clippers if you are running a small-scale barber shop (and for sure if you're a DIYer for you and your family to save a couple of bucks at the barber) but if you're a professional giving haircuts all day long, go for the Classic 76.

You can buy ones for even longer hair lengths but I found that beyond a certain length (like beyond 1 inch) you're better off using scissors since hair bends and scrunches up before it hits the cutting teeth and thus doesn't extend to full length enough to be cut off at the desired 1&#34;. So I use scissors on top, electric shears everywhere else.<br /><br />Shears are essential if you want to maintain short hair.
